Objective\nDevelop a comprehensive web application named 'SmartHomeManager' using Python, with data managed through local text files. The application enables users to manage smart home devices, control them remotely, set automation rules, and monitor energy consumption. Note that the website should start from the Dashboard page.\n\n## 2. Language\nThe required development language for the 'SmartHomeManager' application is Python.\n\n## 3. Page Design\n\nThe 'SmartHomeManager' web application will consist of the following seven pages:\n\n### 1. Dashboard Page\n- **Page Title**: Smart Home Dashboard\n- **Overview**: The main hub displaying overview of all devices, quick controls, and navigation to all functionality.\n- **Elements**:\n  - **ID: dashboard-page** - Type: Div - Container for the dashboard page.\n  - **ID: device-summary** - Type: Div - Summary showing total devices, active devices, and offline devices count.\n  - **ID: device-list-button** - Type: Button - Button to navigate to device list page.\n  - **ID: add-device-button** - Type: Button - Button to navigate to add device page.\n  - **ID: automation-button** - Type: Button - Button to navigate to automation rules page.\n  - **ID: energy-button** - Type: Button - Button to navigate to energy report page.\n  - **ID: activity-button** - Type: Button - Button to navigate to activity logs page.\n  - **ID: room-list** - Type: Div - List of all rooms with device counts, displayed as a dashboard section.\n\n### 2. Device List Page\n- **Page Title**: My Devices\n- **Overview**: A page displaying all registered smart devices with their status and quick controls.\n- **Elements**:\n  - **ID: device-list-page** - Type: Div - Container for the device list page.\n  - **ID: device-table** - Type: Table - Table displaying all devices with name, type, room, status, and actions.\n  - **ID: control-device-button-{device_id}** - Type: Button - Button to navigate to device control page (each row has this button).\n  - **ID: back-to-dashboard** - Type: Button - Button to navigate back to dashboard.\n\n### 3. Device Control Page\n- **Page Title**: Device Control\n- **Overview**: A page for controlling a specific device with detailed settings.\n- **Elements**:\n  - **ID: device-control-page** - Type: Div - Container for the device control page.\n  - **ID: device-name-display** - Type: H2 - Display device name.\n  - **ID: device-status-display** - Type: Div - Display current device status (Online/Offline).\n  - **ID: power-toggle** - Type: Button - Button to toggle device power on/off.\n  - **ID: save-settings-button** - Type: Button - Button to save device settings.\n  - **ID: back-to-devices** - Type: Button - Button to navigate back to device list.\n\n### 5. Automation Rules Page\n- **Page Title**: Automation Rules\n- **Overview**: A page for creating and managing automation rules for devices.\n- **Elements**:\n  - **ID: automation-page** - Type: Div - Container for the automation rules page.\n  - **ID: rules-table** - Type: Table - Table displaying all automation rules with name, trigger, action, and status.\n  - **ID: rule-name** - Type: Input - Field to input rule name.\n  - **ID: trigger-type** - Type: Dropdown - Dropdown to select trigger type (Time, Motion, Temperature).\n  - **ID: trigger-value** - Type: Input - Field to input trigger value (e.g., time or threshold).\n  - **ID: action-device** - Type: Dropdown - Dropdown to select target device.\n  - **ID: action-type** - Type: Dropdown - Dropdown to select action type (Turn On, Turn Off, Set Brightness, Set Temperature).\n  - **ID: add-rule-button** - Type: Button - Button to add new automation rule.\n  - **ID: back-to-dashboard** - Type: Button - Button to navigate back to dashboard.\n\n### 6. Energy Report Page\n- **Page Title**: Energy Report\n- **Overview**: A page displaying energy consumption data and statistics for all devices.\n- **Elements**:\n  - **ID: energy-page** - Type: Div - Container for the energy report page.\n  - **ID: energy-summary** - Type: Div - Summary showing total energy consumption and cost estimate.\n  - **ID: energy-table** - Type: Table - Table displaying energy consumption per device with date and kWh.\n  - **ID: date-filter** - Type: Input (date) - Field to filter energy data by date.\n  - **ID: apply-filter-button** - Type: Button - Button to apply date filter.\n  - **ID: back-to-dashboard** - Type: Button - Button to navigate back to dashboard.\n\n### 7. Activity Logs Page\n- **Page Title**: Activity Logs\n- **Overview**: A page displaying all device activity logs and system events.\n- **Elements**:\n  - **ID: activity-page** - Type: Div - Container for the activity logs page.\n  - **ID: activity-table** - Type: Table - Table displaying activity logs with timestamp, device, action, and details.\n  - **ID: search-activity** - Type: Input - Field to search activity logs.\n  - **ID: apply-search-button** - Type: Button - Button to apply search filter.\n  - **ID: back-to-dashboard** - Type: Button - Button to navigate back to dashboard.\n\n## 4. Data Storage\n\nThe 'SmartHomeManager' application will store data locally in text files organized in the directory 'data'. The following data formats and examples are defined:\n\n### 1. User Data\n- **File Name**: `users.txt`\n- **Data Format**:\n  ```\n  username|email\n  ```\n- **Example Data**:\n  ```\n  john_doe|john@example.com\n  jane_smith|jane@example.com\n  ```\n\n### 2. Device Data\n- **File Name**: `devices.txt`\n- **Data Format**:\n  ```\n  username|device_id|device_name|device_type|room|brand|model|status|power|brightness|temperature|mode|schedule_time\n  ```\n- **Example Data**:\n  ```\n  john_doe|1|Living Room Light|Light|Living Room|Philips|Hue|Online|on|75|||Auto|\n  john_doe|2|Bedroom Thermostat|Thermostat|Bedroom|Nest|Learning|Online|on||72|Auto|22:00\n  jane_smith|3|Kitchen Camera|Camera|Kitchen|Ring|Indoor|Online|on||||Manual|\n  ```\n\n### 3. Room Data\n- **File Name**: `rooms.txt`\n- **Data Format**:\n  ```\n  username|room_id|room_name\n  ```\n- **Example Data**:\n  ```\n  john_doe|1|Living Room\n  john_doe|2|Bedroom\n  john_doe|3|Kitchen\n  jane_smith|1|Living Room\n  ```\n\n### 4. Automation Rules Data\n- **File Name**: `automation_rules.txt`\n- **Data Format**:\n  ```\n  username|rule_id|rule_name|trigger_type|trigger_value|action_device_id|action_type|action_value|enabled\n  ```\n- **Example Data**:\n  ```\n  john_doe|1|Morning Lights|Time|07:00|1|Turn On||true\n  john_doe|2|Night Mode|Time|22:00|1|Set Brightness|20|true\n  jane_smith|1|Motion Alert|Motion|detected|3|Turn On||true\n  ```\n\n### 5. Energy Consumption Logs\n- **File Name**: `energy_logs.txt`\n- **Data Format**:\n  ```\n  username|device_id|date|consumption_kwh\n  ```\n- **Example Data**:\n  ```\n  john_doe|1|2024-11-01|0.5\n  john_doe|2|2024-11-01|2.3\n  john_doe|1|2024-11-02|0.6\n  jane_smith|3|2024-11-01|0.2\n  ```\n\n### 6. Activity Logs\n- **File Name**: `activity_logs.txt`\n- **Data Format**:\n  ```\n  username|timestamp|device_id|action|details\n  ```\n- **Example Data**:\n  ```\n  john_doe|2024-11-01 07:00:00|1|Power On|Automation triggered: Morning Lights\n  john_doe|2024-11-01 08:30:00|2|Settings Changed|Temperature set to 72\n  jane_smith|2024-11-01 09:15:00|3|Power On|Manual control\n  ```\n\nAll files will be saved in the `data` directory to ensure organization and easy access. The format uses a pipe (`|`) delimiter for better readability and parsing. Different types of data will be isolated to ensure efficient data management and retrieval.\n\n",

Objective\nDevelop a comprehensive web application named 'SmartHomeManager' using Python, with data managed through local text files. The application enables users to manage smart home devices, control them remotely, set automation rules, and monitor energy consumption. Note that the website should start from the Dashboard page.\n\n## 2. Language\nThe required development language for the 'SmartHomeManager' application is Python.\n\n## 3. Page Design\n\nThe 'SmartHomeManager' web application will consist of the following seven pages:\n\n### 1. Dashboard Page\n- **Page Title**: Smart Home Dashboard\n- **Overview**: The main hub displaying overview of all devices, quick controls, and navigation to all functionality.\n- **Elements**:\n  - **ID: dashboard-page** - Type: Div - Container for the dashboard page.\n  - **ID: device-summary** - Type: Div - Summary showing total devices, active devices, and offline devices count.\n  - **ID: device-list-button** - Type: Button - Button to navigate to device list page.\n  - **ID: add-device-button** - Type: Button - Button to navigate to add device page.\n  - **ID: automation-button** - Type: Button - Button to navigate to automation rules page.\n  - **ID: energy-button** - Type: Button - Button to navigate to energy report page.\n  - **ID: activity-button** - Type: Button - Button to navigate to activity logs page.\n  - **ID: room-list** - Type: Div - List of all rooms with device counts, displayed as a dashboard section.\n\n### 2. Device List Page\n- **Page Title**: My Devices\n- **Overview**: A page displaying all registered smart devices with their status and quick controls.\n- **Elements**:\n  - **ID: device-list-page** - Type: Div - Container for the device list page.\n  - **ID: device-table** - Type: Table - Table displaying all devices with name, type, room, status, and actions.\n  - **ID: control-device-button-{device_id}** - Type: Button - Button to navigate to device control page (each row has this button).\n  - **ID: back-to-dashboard** - Type: Button - Button to navigate back to dashboard.\n\n### 3. Add Device Page\n- **Page Title**: Add New Device\n- **Overview**: A page for users to register a new smart device.\n- **Elements**:\n  - **ID: add-device-page** - Type: Div - Container for the add device page.\n  - **ID: device-name** - Type: Input - Field to input device name.\n  - **ID: device-type** - Type: Dropdown - Dropdown to select device type (Light, Thermostat, Camera, Lock, Sensor, Appliance).\n  - **ID: device-room** - Type: Dropdown - Dropdown to select room (Living Room, Bedroom, Kitchen, Bathroom, Garage).\n  - **ID: submit-device-button** - Type: Button - Button to submit the new device.\n  - **ID: back-to-dashboard** - Type: Button - Button to navigate back to dashboard.\n\n### 4. Device Control Page\n- **Page Title**: Device Control\n- **Overview**: A page for controlling a specific device with detailed settings.\n- **Elements**:\n  - **ID: device-control-page** - Type: Div - Container for the device control page.\n  - **ID: device-name-display** - Type: H2 - Display device name.\n  - **ID: device-status-display** - Type: Div - Display current device status (Online/Offline).\n  - **ID: power-toggle** - Type: Button - Button to toggle device power on/off.\n  - **ID: save-settings-button** - Type: Button - Button to save device settings.\n  - **ID: back-to-devices** - Type: Button - Button to navigate back to device list.\n\n### 5. Automation Rules Page\n- **Page Title**: Automation Rules\n- **Overview**: A page for creating and managing automation rules for devices.\n- **Elements**:\n  - **ID: automation-page** - Type: Div - Container for the automation rules page.\n  - **ID: rules-table** - Type: Table - Table displaying all automation rules with name, trigger, action, and status.\n  - **ID: rule-name** - Type: Input - Field to input rule name.\n  - **ID: trigger-type** - Type: Dropdown - Dropdown to select trigger type (Time, Motion, Temperature).\n  - **ID: trigger-value** - Type: Input - Field to input trigger value (e.g., time or threshold).\n  - **ID: action-device** - Type: Dropdown - Dropdown to select target device.\n  - **ID: action-type** - Type: Dropdown - Dropdown to select action type (Turn On, Turn Off, Set Brightness, Set Temperature).\n  - **ID: add-rule-button** - Type: Button - Button to add new automation rule.\n  - **ID: back-to-dashboard** - Type: Button - Button to navigate back to dashboard.\n\n### 6. Energy Report Page\n- **Page Title**: Energy Report\n- **Overview**: A page displaying energy consumption data and statistics for all devices.\n- **Elements**:\n  - **ID: energy-page** - Type: Div - Container for the energy report page.\n  - **ID: energy-summary** - Type: Div - Summary showing total energy consumption and cost estimate.\n  - **ID: energy-table** - Type: Table - Table displaying energy consumption per device with date and kWh.\n  - **ID: date-filter** - Type: Input (date) - Field to filter energy data by date.\n  - **ID: apply-filter-button** - Type: Button - Button to apply date filter.\n  - **ID: back-to-dashboard** - Type: Button - Button to navigate back to dashboard.\n\n### 7. Activity Logs Page\n- **Page Title**: Activity Logs\n- **Overview**: A page displaying all device activity logs and system events.\n- **Elements**:\n  - **ID: activity-page** - Type: Div - Container for the activity logs page.\n  - **ID: activity-table** - Type: Table - Table displaying activity logs with timestamp, device, action, and details.\n  - **ID: search-activity** - Type: Input - Field to search activity logs.\n  - **ID: apply-search-button** - Type: Button - Button to apply search filter.\n  - **ID: back-to-dashboard** - Type: Button - Button to navigate back to dashboard.\n\n## 4. Data Storage\n\nThe 'SmartHomeManager' application will store data locally in text files organized in the directory 'data'. The following data formats and examples are defined:\n\n### 1. User Data\n- **File Name**: `users.txt`\n- **Data Format**:\n  ```\n  username|email\n  ```\n- **Example Data**:\n  ```\n  john_doe|john@example.com\n  jane_smith|jane@example.com\n  ```\n\n### 2. Device Data\n- **File Name**: `devices.txt`\n- **Data Format**:\n  ```\n  username|device_id|device_name|device_type|room|brand|model|status|power|brightness|temperature|mode|schedule_time\n  ```\n- **Example Data**:\n  ```\n  john_doe|1|Living Room Light|Light|Living Room|Philips|Hue|Online|on|75|||Auto|\n  john_doe|2|Bedroom Thermostat|Thermostat|Bedroom|Nest|Learning|Online|on||72|Auto|22:00\n  jane_smith|3|Kitchen Camera|Camera|Kitchen|Ring|Indoor|Online|on||||Manual|\n  ```\n\n### 3. Room Data\n- **File Name**: `rooms.txt`\n- **Data Format**:\n  ```\n  username|room_id|room_name\n  ```\n- **Example Data**:\n  ```\n  john_doe|1|Living Room\n  john_doe|2|Bedroom\n  john_doe|3|Kitchen\n  jane_smith|1|Living Room\n  ```\n\n### 4.          === user_task_description ===
         
         # Requirements Document for 'SmartHomeManager' Web Application
         
         ## 1. Objective
         Develop a comprehensive web application named 'SmartHomeManager' using Python, with data managed through local text files. The application enables users to manage smart home devices, control them remotely, set automation rules, and monitor energy consumption. Note that the website should start from the Dashboard page.
         
         ## 2. Language
         The required development language for the 'SmartHomeManager' application is Python.
         
         ## 3. Page Design
         
         The 'SmartHomeManager' web application will consist of the following seven pages:
         
         ### 1. Dashboard Page
         - **Page Title**: Smart Home Dashboard
         - **Overview**: The main hub displaying overview of all devices, quick controls, and navigation to all functionality.
         - **Elements**:
           - **ID: dashboard-page** - Type: Div - Container for the dashboard page.
           - **ID: device-summary** - Type: Div - Summary showing total devices, active devices, and offline devices count.
           - **ID: device-list-button** - Type: Button - Button to navigate to device list page.
           - **ID: add-device-button** - Type: Button - Button to navigate to add device page.
           - **ID: automation-button** - Type: Button - Button to navigate to automation rules page.
           - **ID: energy-button** - Type: Button - Button to navigate to energy report page.
           - **ID: activity-button** - Type: Button - Button to navigate to activity logs page.
           - **ID: room-list** - Type: Div - List of all rooms with device counts, displayed as a dashboard section.
         
         ### 2. Device List Page
         - **Page Title**: My Devices
         - **Overview**: A page displaying all registered smart devices with their status and quick controls.
         - **Elements**:
           - **ID: device-list-page** - Type: Div - Container for the device list page.
           - **ID: device-table** - Type: Table - Table displaying all devices with name, type, room, status, and actions.
           - **ID: control-device-button-{device_id}** - Type: Button - Button to navigate to device control page (each row has this button).
           - **ID: back-to-dashboard** - Type: Button - Button to navigate back to dashboard.
         
         ### 3. Add Device Page
         - **Page Title**: Add New Device
         - **Overview**: A page for users to register a new smart device.
         - **Elements**:
           - **ID: add-device-page** - Type: Div - Container for the add device page.
           - **ID: device-name** - Type: Input - Field to input device name.
           - **ID: device-type** - Type: Dropdown - Dropdown to select device type (Light, Thermostat, Camera, Lock, Sensor, Appliance).
           - **ID: device-room** - Type: Dropdown - Dropdown to select room (Living Room, Bedroom, Kitchen, Bathroom, Garage).
           - **ID: submit-device-button** - Type: Button - Button to submit the new device.
           - **ID: back-to-dashboard** - Type: Button - Button to navigate back to dashboard.
         
         ### 4. Device Control Page
         - **Page Title**: Device Control
         - **Overview**: A page for controlling a specific device with detailed settings.
         - **Elements**:
           - **ID: device-control-page** - Type: Div - Container for the device control page.
           - **ID: device-name-display** - Type: H2 - Display device name.
           - **ID: device-status-display** - Type: Div - Display current device status (Online/Offline).
           - **ID: power-toggle** - Type: Button - Button to toggle device power on/off.
           - **ID: save-settings-button** - Type: Button - Button to save device settings.
           - **ID: back-to-devices** - Type: Button - Button to navigate back to device list.
         
         ### 5. Automation Rules Page
         - **Page Title**: Automation Rules
         - **Overview**: A page for creating and managing automation rules for devices.
         - **Elements**:
           - **ID: automation-page** - Type: Div - Container for the automation rules page.
           - **ID: rules-table** - Type: Table - Table displaying all automation rules with name, trigger, action, and status.
           - **ID: rule-name** - Type: Input - Field to input rule name.
           - **ID: trigger-type** - Type: Dropdown - Dropdown to select trigger type (Time, Motion, Temperature).
           - **ID: trigger-value** - Type: Input - Field to input trigger value (e.g., time or threshold).
           - **ID: action-device** - Type: Dropdown - Dropdown to select target device.
           - **ID: action-type** - Type: Dropdown - Dropdown to select action type (Turn On, Turn Off, Set Brightness, Set Temperature).
           - **ID: add-rule-button** - Type: Button - Button to add new automation rule.
           - **ID: back-to-dashboard** - Type: Button - Button to navigate back to dashboard.
         
         ### 6. Energy Report Page
         - **Page Title**: Energy Report
         - **Overview**: A page displaying energy consumption data and statistics for all devices.
         - **Elements**:
           - **ID: energy-page** - Type: Div - Container for the energy report page.
           - **ID: energy-summary** - Type: Div - Summary showing total energy consumption and cost estimate.
           - **ID: energy-table** - Type: Table - Table displaying energy consumption per device with date and kWh.
           - **ID: date-filter** - Type: Input (date) - Field to filter energy data by date.
           - **ID: apply-filter-button** - Type: Button - Button to apply date filter.
           - **ID: back-to-dashboard** - Type: Button - Button to navigate back to dashboard.
         
         ### 7. Activity Logs Page
         - **Page Title**: Activity Logs
         - **Overview**: A page displaying all device activity logs and system events.
         - **Elements**:
           - **ID: activity-page** - Type: Div - Container for the activity logs page.
           - **ID: activity-table** - Type: Table - Table displaying activity logs with timestamp, device, action, and details.
           - **ID: search-activity** - Type: Input - Field to search activity logs.
           - **ID: apply-search-button** - Type: Button - Button to apply search filter.
           - **ID: back-to-dashboard** - Type: Button - Button to navigate back to dashboard.
         
         ## 4. Data Storage
         
         The 'SmartHomeManager' application will store data locally in text files organized in the directory 'data'. The following data formats and examples are defined:
         
         ### 1. User Data
         - **File Name**: `users.txt`
         - **Data Format**:
           ```
           username|email
           ```
         - **Example Data**:
           ```
           john_doe|john@example.com
           jane_smith|jane@example.com
           ```
         
         ### 2. Device Data
         - **File Name**: `devices.txt`
         - **Data Format**:
           ```
           username|device_id|device_name|device_type|room|brand|model|status|power|brightness|temperature|mode|schedule_time
           ```
         - **Example Data**:
           ```
           john_doe|1|Living Room Light|Light|Living Room|Philips|Hue|Online|on|75|||Auto|
           john_doe|2|Bedroom Thermostat|Thermostat|Bedroom|Nest|Learning|Online|on||72|Auto|22:00
           jane_smith|3|Kitchen Camera|Camera|Kitchen|Ring|Indoor|Online|on||||Manual|
           ```
         
         ### 3. Room Data
         - **File Name**: `rooms.txt`
         - **Data Format**:
           ```
           username|room_id|room_name
           ```
         - **Example Data**:
           ```
           john_doe|1|Living Room
           john_doe|2|Bedroom
           john_doe|3|Kitchen
           jane_smith|1|Living Room
           ```
         
         ### 4. Automation Rules Data
         - **File Name**: `automation_rules.txt`
         - **Data Format**:
           ```
           username|rule_id|rule_name|trigger_type|trigger_value|action_device_id|action_type|action_value|enabled
           ```
         - **Example Data**:
           ```
           john_doe|1|Morning Lights|Time|07:00|1|Turn On||true
           john_doe|2|Night Mode|Time|22:00|1|Set Brightness|20|true
           jane_smith|1|Motion Alert|Motion|detected|3|Turn On||true
           ```
         
         ### 5. Energy Consumption Logs
         - **File Name**: `energy_logs.txt`
         - **Data Format**:
           ```
           username|device_id|date|consumption_kwh
           ```
         - **Example Data**:
           ```
           john_doe|1|2024-11-01|0.5
           john_doe|2|2024-11-01|2.3
           john_doe|1|2024-11-02|0.6
           jane_smith|3|2024-11-01|0.2
           ```
         
         ### 6. Activity Logs
         - **File Name**: `activity_logs.txt`
         - **Data Format**:
           ```
           username|timestamp|device_id|action|details
           ```
         - **Example Data**:
           ```
           john_doe|2024-11-01 07:00:00|1|Power On|Automation triggered: Morning Lights
           john_doe|2024-11-01 08:30:00|2|Settings Changed|Temperature set to 72
           jane_smith|2024-11-01 09:15:00|3|Power On|Manual control
           ```
         
         All files will be saved in the `data` directory to ensure organization and easy access. The format uses a pipe (`|`) delimiter for better readability and parsing. Different types of data will be isolated to ensure efficient data management and retrieval.

         === user_task_description ===
         
         # Requirements Document for 'SmartHomeManager' Web Application
         
         ## 1. Objective
         Develop a comprehensive web application named 'SmartHomeManager' using Python, with data managed through local text files. The application enables users to manage smart home devices, control them remotely, set automation rules, and monitor energy consumption. Note that the website should start from the Dashboard page.
         
         ## 2. Language
         The required development language for the 'SmartHomeManager' application is Python.
         
         ## 3. Page Design
         
         The 'SmartHomeManager' web application will consist of the following seven pages:
         
         ### 1. Dashboard Page
         - **Page Title**: Smart Home Dashboard
         - **Overview**: The main hub displaying overview of all devices, quick controls, and navigation to all functionality.
         - **Elements**:
           - **ID: dashboard-page** - Type: Div - Container for the dashboard page.
           - **ID: device-summary** - Type: Div - Summary showing total devices, active devices, and offline devices count.
           - **ID: device-list-button** - Type: Button - Button to navigate to device list page.
           - **ID: add-device-button** - Type: Button - Button to navigate to add device page.
           - **ID: automation-button** - Type: Button - Button to navigate to automation rules page.
           - **ID: energy-button** - Type: Button - Button to navigate to energy report page.
           - **ID: activity-button** - Type: Button - Button to navigate to activity logs page.
           - **ID: room-list** - Type: Div - List of all rooms with device counts, displayed as a dashboard section.
         
         ### 2. Device List Page
         - **Page Title**: My Devices
         - **Overview**: A page displaying all registered smart devices with their status and quick controls.
         - **Elements**:
           - **ID: device-list-page** - Type: Div - Container for the device list page.
           - **ID: device-table** - Type: Table - Table displaying all devices with name, type, room, status, and actions.
           - **ID: control-device-button-{device_id}** - Type: Button - Button to navigate to device control page (each row has this button).
           - **ID: back-to-dashboard** - Type: Button - Button to navigate back to dashboard.
         
         ### 3. Add Device Page
         - **Page Title**: Add New Device
         - **Overview**: A page for users to register a new smart device.
         - **Elements**:
           - **ID: add-device-page** - Type: Div - Container for the add device page.
           - **ID: device-name** - Type: Input - Field to input device name.
           - **ID: device-type** - Type: Dropdown - Dropdown to select device type (Light, Thermostat, Camera, Lock, Sensor, Appliance).
           - **ID: device-room** - Type: Dropdown - Dropdown to select room (Living Room, Bedroom, Kitchen, Bathroom, Garage).
           - **ID: submit-device-button** - Type: Button - Button to submit the new device.
           - **ID: back-to-dashboard** - Type: Button - Button to navigate back to dashboard.
         
         ### 4. Device Control Page
         - **Page Title**: Device Control
         - **Overview**: A page for controlling a specific device with detailed settings.
         - **Elements**:
           - **ID: device-control-page** - Type: Div - Container for the device control page.
           - **ID: device-name-display** - Type: H2 - Display device name.
           - **ID: device-status-display** - Type: Div - Display current device status (Online/Offline).
           - **ID: power-toggle** - Type: Button - Button to toggle device power on/off.
           - **ID: save-settings-button** - Type: Button - Button to save device settings.
           - **ID: back-to-devices** - Type: Button - Button to navigate back to device list.
         
         ### 5. Automation Rules Page
         - **Page Title**: Automation Rules
         - **Overview**: A page for creating and managing automation rules for devices.
         - **Elements**:
           - **ID: automation-page** - Type: Div - Container for the automation rules page.
           - **ID: rules-table** - Type: Table - Table displaying all automation rules with name, trigger, action, and status.
           - **ID: rule-name** - Type: Input - Field to input rule name.
           - **ID: trigger-type** - Type: Dropdown - Dropdown to select trigger type (Time, Motion, Temperature).
           - **ID: trigger-value** - Type: Input - Field to input trigger value (e.g., time or threshold).
           - **ID: action-device** - Type: Dropdown - Dropdown to select target device.
           - **ID: action-type** - Type: Dropdown - Dropdown to select action type (Turn On, Turn Off, Set Brightness, Set Temperature).
           - **ID: add-rule-button** - Type: Button - Button to add new automation rule.
           - **ID: back-to-dashboard** - Type: Button - Button to navigate back to dashboard.
         
         ### 6. Energy Report Page
         - **Page Title**: Energy Report
         - **Overview**: A page displaying energy consumption data and statistics for all devices.
         - **Elements**:
           - **ID: energy-page** - Type: Div - Container for the energy report page.
           - **ID: energy-summary** - Type: Div - Summary showing total energy consumption and cost estimate.
           - **ID: energy-table** - Type: Table - Table displaying energy consumption per device with date and kWh.
           - **ID: date-filter** - Type: Input (date) - Field to filter energy data by date.
           - **ID: apply-filter-button** - Type: Button - Button to apply date filter.
           - **ID: back-to-dashboard** - Type: Button - Button to navigate back to dashboard.
         
         ### 7. Activity Logs Page
         - **Page Title**: Activity Logs
         - **Overview**: A page displaying all device activity logs and system events.
         - **Elements**:
           - **ID: activity-page** - Type: Div - Container for the activity logs page.
           - **ID: activity-table** - Type: Table - Table displaying activity logs with timestamp, device, action, and details.
           - **ID: search-activity** - Type: Input - Field to search activity logs.
           - **ID: apply-search-button** - Type: Button - Button to apply search filter.
           - **ID: back-to-dashboard** - Type: Button - Button to navigate back to dashboard.
         
         ## 4. Data Storage
         
         The 'SmartHomeManager' application will store data locally in text files organized in the directory 'data'. The following data formats and examples are defined:
         
         ### 1. User Data
         - **File Name**: `users.txt`
         - **Data Format**:
           ```
           username|email
           ```
         - **Example Data**:
           ```
           john_doe|john@example.com
           jane_smith|jane@example.com
           ```
         
         ### 2. Device Data
         - **File Name**: `devices.txt`
         - **Data Format**:
           ```
           username|device_id|device_name|device_type|room|brand|model|status|power|brightness|temperature|mode|schedule_time
           ```
         - **Example Data**:
           ```
           john_doe|1|Living Room Light|Light|Living Room|Philips|Hue|Online|on|75|||Auto|
           john_doe|2|Bedroom Thermostat|Thermostat|Bedroom|Nest|Learning|Online|on||72|Auto|22:00
           jane_smith|3|Kitchen Camera|Camera|Kitchen|Ring|Indoor|Online|on||||Manual|
           ```
         
         ### 3. Room Data
         - **File Name**: `rooms.txt`
         - **Data Format**:
           ```
           username|room_id|room_name
           ```
         - **Example Data**:
           ```
           john_doe|1|Living Room
           john_doe|2|Bedroom
           john_doe|3|Kitchen
           jane_smith|1|Living Room
           ```
         
         ### 4. Automation Rules Data
         - **File Name**: `automation_rules.txt`
         - **Data Format**:
           ```
           username|rule_id|rule_name|trigger_type|trigger_value|action_device_id|action_type|action_value|enabled
           ```
         - **Example Data**:
           ```
           john_doe|1|Morning Lights|Time|07:00|1|Turn On||true
           john_doe|2|Night Mode|Time|22:00|1|Set Brightness|20|true
           jane_smith|1|Motion Alert|Motion|detected|3|Turn On||true
           ```
         
         ### 5. Energy Consumption Logs
         - **File Name**: `energy_logs.txt`
         - **Data Format**:
           ```
           username|device_id|date|consumption_kwh
           ```
         - **Example Data**:
           ```
           john_doe|1|2024-11-01|0.5
           john_doe|2|2024-11-01|2.3
           john_doe|1|2024-11-02|0.6
           jane_smith|3|2024-11-01|0.2
           ```
         
         ### 6. Activity Logs
         - **File Name**: `activity_logs.txt`
         - **Data Format**:
           ```
           username|timestamp|device_id|action|details
           ```
         - **Example Data**:
           ```
           john_doe|2024-11-01 07:00:00|1|Power On|Automation triggered: Morning Lights
           john_doe|2024-11-01 08:30:00|2|Settings Changed|Temperature set to 72
           jane_smith|2024-11-01 09:15:00|3|Power On|Manual control
           ```
         
         All files will be saved in the `data` directory to ensure organization and easy access. The format uses a pipe (`|`) delimiter for better readability and parsing. Different types of data will be isolated to ensure efficient data management and retrieval.

         from flask import Flask, render_template, redirect, url_for, request
         import os
         
         app = Flask(__name__)
         app.config['SECRET_KEY'] = 'dev-secret-key'
         
         DATA_DIR = 'data'
         
         # Utility functions for data file handling
         
         def read_devices(username=None):
             devices = []
             filepath = os.path.join(DATA_DIR, 'devices.txt')
             try:
                 with open(filepath, 'r', encoding='utf-8') as f:
                     for line in f:
                         parts = line.strip().split('|')
                         if len(parts) < 13:
                             continue  # skip malformed lines
                         d = {
                             'username': parts[0],
                             'device_id': int(parts[1]),
                             'device_name': parts[2],
                             'device_type': parts[3],
                             'room': parts[4],
                             'brand': parts[5],
                             'model': parts[6],
                             'status': parts[7],
                             'power': parts[8],
                             'brightness': parts[9],
                             'temperature': parts[10],
                             'mode': parts[11],
                             'schedule_time': parts[12],
                         }
                         if username is None or d['username'] == username:
                             devices.append(d)
             except FileNotFoundError:
                 pass
             return devices
         
         
         def save_devices(devices):
             filepath = os.path.join(DATA_DIR, 'devices.txt')
             try:
                 with open(filepath, 'w', encoding='utf-8') as f:
                     for d in devices:
                         line = '|'.join([
                             d['username'],
                             str(d['device_id']),
                             d['device_name'],
                             d['device_type'],
                             d['room'],
                             d['brand'],
                             d['model'],
                             d['status'],
                             d['power'],
                             d['brightness'],
                             d['temperature'],
                             d['mode'],
                             d['schedule_time']]) + '\n'
                         f.write(line)
             except Exception:
                 pass
         
         
         def read_rooms(username=None):
             rooms = []
             filepath = os.path.join(DATA_DIR, 'rooms.txt')
             try:
                 with open(filepath, 'r', encoding='utf-8') as f:
                     for line in f:
                         parts = line.strip().split('|')
                         if len(parts) < 3:
                             continue
                         r = {
                             'username': parts[0],
                             'room_id': int(parts[1]),
                             'room_name': parts[2],
                         }
                         if username is None or r['username'] == username:
                             rooms.append(r)
             except FileNotFoundError:
                 pass
             return rooms
         
         
         def read_automation_rules(username=None):
             rules = []
             filepath = os.path.join(DATA_DIR, 'automation_rules.txt')
             try:
                 with open(filepath, 'r', encoding='utf-8') as f:
                     for line in f:
                         parts = line.strip().split('|')
                         if len(parts) < 9:
                             continue
                         rule = {
                             'username': parts[0],
                             'rule_id': int(parts[1]),
                             'rule_name': parts[2],
                             'trigger_type': parts[3],
                             'trigger_value': parts[4],
                             'action_device_id': int(parts[5]),
                             'action_type': parts[6],
                             'action_value': parts[7],
                             'enabled': parts[8].lower() == 'true'
                         }
                         if username is None or rule['username'] == username:
                             rules.append(rule)
             except FileNotFoundError:
                 pass
             return rules
         
         
         def save_automation_rules(rules):
             filepath = os.path.join(DATA_DIR, 'automation_rules.txt')
             try:
                 with open(filepath, 'w', encoding='utf-8') as f:
                     for r in rules:
                         line = '|'.join([
                             r['username'],
                             str(r['rule_id']),
                             r['rule_name'],
                             r['trigger_type'],
                             r['trigger_value'],
                             str(r['action_device_id']),
                             r['action_type'],
                             r['action_value'],
                             'true' if r['enabled'] else 'false'
                         ]) + '\n'
                         f.write(line)
             except Exception:
                 pass
         
         
         def read_energy_logs(username=None):
             records = []
             filepath = os.path.join(DATA_DIR, 'energy_logs.txt')
             try:
                 with open(filepath, 'r', encoding='utf-8') as f:
                     for line in f:
                         parts = line.strip().split('|')
                         if len(parts) < 4:
                             continue
                         record = {
                             'username': parts[0],
                             'device_id': int(parts[1]),
                             'date': parts[2],
                             'consumption_kwh': float(parts[3]),
                         }
                         if username is None or record['username'] == username:
                             records.append(record)
             except FileNotFoundError:
                 pass
             return records
         
         
         def read_activity_logs(username=None):
             logs = []
             filepath = os.path.join(DATA_DIR, 'activity_logs.txt')
             try:
                 with open(filepath, 'r', encoding='utf-8') as f:
                     for line in f:
                         parts = line.strip().split('|')
                         if len(parts) < 5:
                             continue
                         log = {
                             'username': parts[0],
                             'timestamp': parts[1],
                             'device_id': int(parts[2]),
                             'action': parts[3],
                             'details': parts[4],
                         }
                         if username is None or log['username'] == username:
                             logs.append(log)
             except FileNotFoundError:
                 pass
             return logs
         
         
         # Helper for unique ids
         
         def get_next_device_id(devices):
             if not devices:
                 return 1
             return max(d['device_id'] for d in devices) + 1
         
         def get_next_rule_id(rules):
             if not rules:
                 return 1
             return max(r['rule_id'] for r in rules) + 1
         
         
         # Application default user
         DEFAULT_USERNAME = 'john_doe'
         
         
         # 1. Root Route
         @app.route('/', methods=['GET'])
         def root_redirect():
             return redirect(url_for('dashboard'))
         
         
         # 2. Dashboard Page
         @app.route('/dashboard', methods=['GET'])
         def dashboard():
             username = DEFAULT_USERNAME
             devices = read_devices(username)
             rooms = read_rooms(username)
         
             total_devices = len(devices)
             active_devices = sum(1 for d in devices if d['status'].lower() == 'online')
             offline_devices = total_devices - active_devices
         
             # Room name to device count
             rooms_count = {}
             for r in rooms:
                 rooms_count[r['room_name']] = 0
             for d in devices:
                 if d['room'] in rooms_count:
                     rooms_count[d['room']] += 1
         
             return render_template('dashboard.html',
                                    total_devices=total_devices,
                                    active_devices=active_devices,
                                    offline_devices=offline_devices,
                                    rooms=rooms_count)
         
         
         # 3. Device List Page
         @app.route('/devices', methods=['GET'])
         def device_list():
             username = DEFAULT_USERNAME
             devices_all = read_devices(username)
             # Provide only keys required by page
             devices = []
             for d in devices_all:
                 devices.append({
                     'device_id': d['device_id'],
                     'device_name': d['device_name'],
                     'device_type': d['device_type'],
                     'room': d['room'],
                     'status': d['status'],
                 })
             return render_template('device_list.html', devices=devices)
         
         
         # 4. Add Device Page
         @app.route('/device/add', methods=['GET', 'POST'])
         def add_device():
             username = DEFAULT_USERNAME
             device_types = set()
             rooms_list = []
         
             devices_all = read_devices(username)
             rooms = read_rooms(username)
         
             # Get unique device types from existing devices
             for d in devices_all:
                 device_types.add(d['device_type'])
             device_types = sorted(device_types)
         
             # Get list of room names
             rooms_list = sorted({r['room_name'] for r in rooms})
         
             if request.method == 'POST':
                 device_name = request.form.get('device_name', '').strip()
                 device_type = request.form.get('device_type', '').strip()
                 room = request.form.get('device_room', '').strip()
         
                 # Validate required fields
                 if not device_name or not device_type or not room:
                     # Re-render with error? Spec does not mention error handling. Just return.
                     return render_template('add_device.html', device_types=device_types, rooms=rooms_list)
         
                 # Assign new device_id
                 new_id = get_next_device_id(devices_all)
         
                 # Default values for new device
                 brand = ''
                 model = ''
                 status = 'Offline'
                 power = 'off'
                 brightness = ''
                 temperature = ''
                 mode = ''
                 schedule_time = ''
         
                 new_device = {
                     'username': username,
                     'device_id': new_id,
                     'device_name': device_name,
                     'device_type': device_type,
                     'room': room,
                     'brand': brand,
                     'model': model,
                     'status': status,
                     'power': power,
                     'brightness': brightness,
                     'temperature': temperature,
                     'mode': mode,
                     'schedule_time': schedule_time,
                 }
         
                 devices_all.append(new_device)
                 save_devices(devices_all)
         
                 return redirect(url_for('device_list'))
         
             # GET method
             return render_template('add_device.html', device_types=device_types, rooms=rooms_list)
         
         
         # 5. Device Control Page
         @app.route('/device/<int:device_id>/control', methods=['GET', 'POST'])
         def device_control(device_id):
             username = DEFAULT_USERNAME
             devices_all = read_devices(username)
             device = None
             for d in devices_all:
                 if d['device_id'] == device_id and d['username'] == username:
                     device = d
                     break
             if device is None:
                 # Device not found, redirect to device list
                 return redirect(url_for('device_list'))
         
             if request.method == 'POST':
                 # Update fields from form
                 # Spec does not prescribe exact form fields except power toggle and settings
                 # We will handle power, brightness, temperature, mode, schedule_time if present
         
                 power = request.form.get('power')
                 brightness = request.form.get('brightness', '')
                 temperature = request.form.get('temperature', '')
                 mode = request.form.get('mode', '')
                 schedule_time = request.form.get('schedule_time', '')
         
                 if power in ('on', 'off'):
                     device['power'] = power
                     device['status'] = 'Online' if power == 'on' else 'Offline'
         
                 # Update optional fields if provided
                 device['brightness'] = brightness
                 device['temperature'] = temperature
                 device['mode'] = mode
                 device['schedule_time'] = schedule_time
         
                 # Save back
                 save_devices(devices_all)
         
                 # After POST, redirect to same control page (reload)
                 return redirect(url_for('device_control', device_id=device_id))
         
             # GET method
             # Provide required keys plus all available for template
             device_ctx = {
                 'device_id': device['device_id'],
                 'device_name': device['device_name'],
                 'status': device['status'],
                 'power': device['power'],
                 'brightness': device['brightness'],
                 'temperature': device['temperature'],
                 'mode': device['mode'],
                 'schedule_time': device['schedule_time'],
             }
         
             return render_template('device_control.html', device=device_ctx)
         
         
         # 6. Automation Rules Page
         @app.route('/automation', methods=['GET', 'POST'])
         def automation():
             username = DEFAULT_USERNAME
             rules = read_automation_rules(username)
             devices_all = read_devices(username)
         
             if request.method == 'POST':
                 # Add or update rules - the spec does not clarify update details so we'll assume add only
         
                 rule_name = request.form.get('rule_name', '').strip()
                 trigger_type = request.form.get('trigger_type', '').strip()
                 trigger_value = request.form.get('trigger_value', '').strip()
                 action_device_id_str = request.form.get('action_device', '').strip()
                 action_type = request.form.get('action_type', '').strip()
         
                 if not rule_name or not trigger_type or not action_device_id_str or not action_type:
                     # Missing required fields, re-render
                     pass  # Just continue to render with existing
                 else:
                     try:
                         action_device_id = int(action_device_id_str)
                     except ValueError:
                         action_device_id = None
         
                     if action_device_id is not None:
                         # New rule_id
                         new_id = get_next_rule_id(rules)
                         new_rule = {
                             'username': username,
                             'rule_id': new_id,
                             'rule_name': rule_name,
                             'trigger_type': trigger_type,
                             'trigger_value': trigger_value,
                             'action_device_id': action_device_id,
                             'action_type': action_type,
                             'action_value': '',
                             'enabled': True
                         }
                         rules.append(new_rule)
                         save_automation_rules(rules)
                         return redirect(url_for('automation'))
         
             # GET or default render
             # provide devices with device_id and device_name
             devices = [{'device_id': d['device_id'], 'device_name': d['device_name']} for d in devices_all]
         
             return render_template('automation.html', automation_rules=rules, devices=devices)
         
         
         # 7. Energy Report Page
         @app.route('/energy', methods=['GET'])
         def energy():
             username = DEFAULT_USERNAME
             energy_records = read_energy_logs(username)
             devices = read_devices(username)
         
             # Enrich energy_records with device_name
             device_name_map = {d['device_id']: d['device_name'] for d in devices}
         
             # Optional date filter
             date_filter = request.args.get('date_filter', None)
         
             filtered_records = []
             for r in energy_records:
                 if date_filter and r['date'] != date_filter:
                     continue
                 dev_name = device_name_map.get(r['device_id'], '')
                 rec = {
                     'username': r['username'],
                     'device_id': r['device_id'],
                     'device_name': dev_name,
                     'date': r['date'],
                     'consumption_kwh': r['consumption_kwh'],
                 }
                 filtered_records.append(rec)
         
             return render_template('energy.html', energy_records=filtered_records, date_filter=date_filter)
         
         
         # 8. Activity Logs Page
         @app.route('/activity', methods=['GET', 'POST'])
         def activity_logs():
             username = DEFAULT_USERNAME
             logs = read_activity_logs(username)
         
             search_query = None
             if request.method == 'POST':
                 search_query = request.form.get('search_query', '').strip()
                 if search_query:
                     logs = [log for log in logs if search_query.lower() in log['action'].lower() or search_query.lower() in log['details'].lower() or search_query.lower() in log['username'].lower()]
         
             return render_template('activity_logs.html', logs=logs, search_query=search_query)
         
         
         if __name__ == '__main__':
             app.run(debug=True, port=5000)

         from flask import Flask, render_template, redirect, url_for, request
         import os
         
         app = Flask(__name__)
         app.config['SECRET_KEY'] = 'dev-secret-key'
         
         DATA_DIR = 'data'
         
         # Data file handling utilities
         
         def read_devices(username=None):
             devices = []
             filepath = os.path.join(DATA_DIR, 'devices.txt')
             try:
                 with open(filepath, 'r', encoding='utf-8') as f:
                     for line in f:
                         parts = line.strip().split('|')
                         if len(parts) < 13:
                             continue
                         device = {
                             'username': parts[0],
                             'device_id': int(parts[1]),
                             'device_name': parts[2],
                             'device_type': parts[3],
                             'room': parts[4],
                             'brand': parts[5],
                             'model': parts[6],
                             'status': parts[7],
                             'power': parts[8],
                             'brightness': parts[9],
                             'temperature': parts[10],
                             'mode': parts[11],
                             'schedule_time': parts[12],
                         }
                         if username is None or device['username'] == username:
                             devices.append(device)
             except FileNotFoundError:
                 pass
             return devices
         
         
         def save_devices(devices):
             filepath = os.path.join(DATA_DIR, 'devices.txt')
             try:
                 with open(filepath, 'w', encoding='utf-8') as f:
                     for d in devices:
                         line = '|'.join([
                             d['username'],
                             str(d['device_id']),
                             d['device_name'],
                             d['device_type'],
                             d['room'],
                             d['brand'],
                             d['model'],
                             d['status'],
                             d['power'],
                             d['brightness'],
                             d['temperature'],
                             d['mode'],
                             d['schedule_time'],
                         ]) + '\n'
                         f.write(line)
             except Exception:
                 pass
         
         
         def read_rooms(username=None):
             rooms = []
             filepath = os.path.join(DATA_DIR, 'rooms.txt')
             try:
                 with open(filepath, 'r', encoding='utf-8') as f:
                     for line in f:
                         parts = line.strip().split('|')
                         if len(parts) < 3:
                             continue
                         room = {
                             'username': parts[0],
                             'room_id': int(parts[1]),
                             'room_name': parts[2],
                         }
                         if username is None or room['username'] == username:
                             rooms.append(room)
             except FileNotFoundError:
                 pass
             return rooms
         
         
         def read_automation_rules(username=None):
             rules = []
             filepath = os.path.join(DATA_DIR, 'automation_rules.txt')
             try:
                 with open(filepath, 'r', encoding='utf-8') as f:
                     for line in f:
                         parts = line.strip().split('|')
                         if len(parts) < 9:
                             continue
                         rule = {
                             'username': parts[0],
                             'rule_id': int(parts[1]),
                             'rule_name': parts[2],
                             'trigger_type': parts[3],
                             'trigger_value': parts[4],
                             'action_device_id': int(parts[5]),
                             'action_type': parts[6],
                             'action_value': parts[7],
                             'enabled': parts[8].lower() == 'true',
                         }
                         if username is None or rule['username'] == username:
                             rules.append(rule)
             except FileNotFoundError:
                 pass
             return rules
         
         
         def save_automation_rules(rules):
             filepath = os.path.join(DATA_DIR, 'automation_rules.txt')
             try:
                 with open(filepath, 'w', encoding='utf-8') as f:
                     for r in rules:
                         line = '|'.join([
                             r['username'],
                             str(r['rule_id']),
                             r['rule_name'],
                             r['trigger_type'],
                             r['trigger_value'],
                             str(r['action_device_id']),
                             r['action_type'],
                             r['action_value'],
                             'true' if r['enabled'] else 'false',
                         ]) + '\n'
                         f.write(line)
             except Exception:
                 pass
         
         
         def read_energy_logs(username=None):
             energy_records = []
             filepath = os.path.join(DATA_DIR, 'energy_logs.txt')
             try:
                 with open(filepath, 'r', encoding='utf-8') as f:
                     for line in f:
                         parts = line.strip().split('|')
                         if len(parts) < 4:
                             continue
                         record = {
                             'username': parts[0],
                             'device_id': int(parts[1]),
                             'date': parts[2],
                             'consumption_kwh': float(parts[3]),
                         }
                         if username is None or record['username'] == username:
                             energy_records.append(record)
             except FileNotFoundError:
                 pass
             return energy_records
         
         
         def read_activity_logs(username=None):
             logs = []
             filepath = os.path.join(DATA_DIR, 'activity_logs.txt')
             try:
                 with open(filepath, 'r', encoding='utf-8') as f:
                     for line in f:
                         parts = line.strip().split('|')
                         if len(parts) < 5:
                             continue
                         log = {
                             'username': parts[0],
                             'timestamp': parts[1],
                             'device_id': int(parts[2]),
                             'action': parts[3],
                             'details': parts[4],
                         }
                         if username is None or log['username'] == username:
                             logs.append(log)
             except FileNotFoundError:
                 pass
             return logs
         
         
         # Helper functions
         
         def get_next_device_id(devices):
             if not devices:
                 return 1
             return max(d['device_id'] for d in devices) + 1
         
         
         def get_next_rule_id(rules):
             if not rules:
                 return 1
             return max(r['rule_id'] for r in rules) + 1
         
         
         DEFAULT_USERNAME = 'john_doe'
         
         
         # 1. Root Route
         @app.route('/', methods=['GET'])
         def root_redirect():
             return redirect(url_for('dashboard'))
         
         
         # 2. Dashboard Page
         @app.route('/dashboard', methods=['GET'])
         def dashboard():
             username = DEFAULT_USERNAME
             devices = read_devices(username)
             rooms = read_rooms(username)
         
             total_devices = len(devices)
             active_devices = sum(1 for d in devices if d['status'].lower() == 'online')
             offline_devices = total_devices - active_devices
         
             room_device_counts = {r['room_name']: 0 for r in rooms}
             for d in devices:
                 if d['room'] in room_device_counts:
                     room_device_counts[d['room']] += 1
         
             return render_template(
                 'dashboard.html',
                 total_devices=total_devices,
                 active_devices=active_devices,
                 offline_devices=offline_devices,
                 rooms=room_device_counts
             )
         
         
         # 3. Device List Page
         @app.route('/devices', methods=['GET'])
         def device_list():
             username = DEFAULT_USERNAME
             all_devices = read_devices(username)
             devices = [
                 {
                     'device_id': d['device_id'],
                     'device_name': d['device_name'],
                     'device_type': d['device_type'],
                     'room': d['room'],
                     'status': d['status'],
                 } for d in all_devices
             ]
             return render_template('device_list.html', devices=devices)
         
         
         # 4. Add Device Page
         @app.route('/device/add', methods=['GET', 'POST'])
         def add_device():
             username = DEFAULT_USERNAME
             devices = read_devices(username)
             rooms = read_rooms(username)
         
             device_types = sorted(set(d['device_type'] for d in devices))
             room_names = sorted(set(r['room_name'] for r in rooms))
         
             if request.method == 'POST':
                 device_name = request.form.get('device_name', '').strip()
                 device_type = request.form.get('device_type', '').strip()
                 room = request.form.get('device_room', '').strip()
         
                 if not device_name or not device_type or not room:
                     # Missing required fields, just re-render GET with lists
                     return render_template('add_device.html', device_types=device_types, rooms=room_names)
         
                 new_device_id = get_next_device_id(devices)
         
                 new_device = {
                     'username': username,
                     'device_id': new_device_id,
                     'device_name': device_name,
                     'device_type': device_type,
                     'room': room,
                     'brand': '',
                     'model': '',
                     'status': 'Offline',
                     'power': 'off',
                     'brightness': '',
                     'temperature': '',
                     'mode': '',
                     'schedule_time': '',
                 }
         
                 devices.append(new_device)
                 save_devices(devices)
         
                 return redirect(url_for('device_list'))
         
             # GET method
             return render_template('add_device.html', device_types=device_types, rooms=room_names)
         
         
         # 5. Device Control Page
         @app.route('/device/<int:device_id>/control', methods=['GET', 'POST'])
         def device_control(device_id):
             username = DEFAULT_USERNAME
             devices = read_devices(username)
             device = next((d for d in devices if d['device_id'] == device_id and d['username'] == username), None)
             if device is None:
                 return redirect(url_for('device_list'))
         
             if request.method == 'POST':
                 power = request.form.get('power')
                 brightness = request.form.get('brightness', '')
                 temperature = request.form.get('temperature', '')
                 mode = request.form.get('mode', '')
                 schedule_time = request.form.get('schedule_time', '')
         
                 if power in ('on', 'off'):
                     device['power'] = power
                     device['status'] = 'Online' if power == 'on' else 'Offline'
         
                 device['brightness'] = brightness
                 device['temperature'] = temperature
                 device['mode'] = mode
                 device['schedule_time'] = schedule_time
         
                 save_devices(devices)
         
                 return redirect(url_for('device_control', device_id=device_id))
         
             device_context = {
                 'device_id': device['device_id'],
                 'device_name': device['device_name'],
                 'status': device['status'],
                 'power': device['power'],
                 'brightness': device['brightness'],
                 'temperature': device['temperature'],
                 'mode': device['mode'],
                 'schedule_time': device['schedule_time'],
             }
             return render_template('device_control.html', device=device_context)
         
         
         # 6. Automation Rules Page
         @app.route('/automation', methods=['GET', 'POST'])
         def automation():
             username = DEFAULT_USERNAME
             rules = read_automation_rules(username)
             devices = read_devices(username)
         
             if request.method == 'POST':
                 rule_name = request.form.get('rule_name', '').strip()
                 trigger_type = request.form.get('trigger_type', '').strip()
                 trigger_value = request.form.get('trigger_value', '').strip()
                 action_device_id_str = request.form.get('action_device', '').strip()
                 action_type = request.form.get('action_type', '').strip()
         
                 if rule_name and trigger_type and action_device_id_str.isdigit() and action_type:
                     action_device_id = int(action_device_id_str)
                     new_rule_id = get_next_rule_id(rules)
                     new_rule = {
                         'username': username,
                         'rule_id': new_rule_id,
                         'rule_name': rule_name,
                         'trigger_type': trigger_type,
                         'trigger_value': trigger_value,
                         'action_device_id': action_device_id,
                         'action_type': action_type,
                         'action_value': '',  # Empty as per spec
                         'enabled': True
                     }
                     rules.append(new_rule)
                     save_automation_rules(rules)
                     return redirect(url_for('automation'))
         
             device_select_list = [{'device_id': d['device_id'], 'device_name': d['device_name']} for d in devices]
             return render_template('automation.html', automation_rules=rules, devices=device_select_list)
         
         
         # 7. Energy Report Page
         @app.route('/energy', methods=['GET'])
         def energy():
             username = DEFAULT_USERNAME
             energy_records = read_energy_logs(username)
             devices = read_devices(username)
         
             device_name_map = {d['device_id']: d['device_name'] for d in devices}
         
             date_filter = request.args.get('date_filter')
         
             filtered_records = []
             for record in energy_records:
                 if date_filter and record['date'] != date_filter:
                     continue
                 filtered_records.append({
                     'username': record['username'],
                     'device_id': record['device_id'],
                     'device_name': device_name_map.get(record['device_id'], ''),
                     'date': record['date'],
                     'consumption_kwh': record['consumption_kwh'],
                 })
         
             return render_template('energy.html', energy_records=filtered_records, date_filter=date_filter)
         
         
         # 8. Activity Logs Page
         @app.route('/activity', methods=['GET', 'POST'])
         def activity_logs():
             username = DEFAULT_USERNAME
             logs = read_activity_logs(username)
         
             search_query = None
             if request.method == 'POST':
                 search_query = request.form.get('search_query', '').strip()
                 if search_query:
                     logs = [log for log in logs if search_query.lower() in log['action'].lower() or search_query.lower() in log['details'].lower() or search_query.lower() in log['username'].lower()]
         
             return render_template('activity_logs.html', logs=logs, search_query=search_query)
         
         
         if __name__ == '__main__':
             app.run(debug=True, port=5000)
